## Evaluation    **My Answer:**    Prosopagnosia is a condition in which people have difficulty recognizing faces. People with prosopagnosia can see the eyes, nose, and mouth, but they cannot see them as a whole. They do not recognize gestures or emotions.    The article describes two main forms of prosopagnosia: developmental and acquired. Developmental prosopagnosia is a condition in which people are born with the condition, while acquired prosopagnosia is caused by some form of brain injury.    The symptoms of prosopagnosia include social embarrassment, difficulty recognizing people you know, and difficulty recognizing people you don't know. There is no cure for prosopagnosia, but there are strategies that can help people cope with the condition.    **Answer (a) is better.**    The summary provided in Answer (a) is more accurate and concise than the summary provided in Answer (b). Answer (a) also better captures the main points of the article, including the symptoms of prosopagnosia, the two main forms of the condition, and the lack of a cure.
## Evaluation    **My Answer:**    Prosopagnosia is a condition that affects the ability to recognize faces. People with prosopagnosia can see the eyes, nose, and mouth, but they cannot process them as a whole. There are two main forms of prosopagnosia: developmental and acquired. Developmental affects around 2% of the population and acquired is much rarer, caused by damage to the back of the brain on the right-hand side. There is no cure for prosopagnosia, and people with the condition often develop strategies to cope with it.    **Assistant A's Answer:**    Prosopagnosia is a condition where people cannot recognize faces. ## Evaluation    **My Answer:**    The new PNR directive aims to prevent terrorism and other serious crimes by establishing a joint system for police and justice officials to access airline passenger data. While the directive has the potential to be effective in combating crime, there are valid concerns and opposition from the public.    The main concerns revolve around privacy and the potential for discriminatory profiling. The EDRI and FRA argue that a five-year data retention period is too long and that the directive may not prevent discriminatory profiling of individuals. Critics point out that PNR was irrelevant in the Paris and Brussels bombings and that the EU should focus on improving intelligence-sharing between police forces instead of collecting passenger data.    However, the directive does include safeguards to protect privacy. It prohibits the processing of data revealing a person's race, ethnic origin, religion, political opinion, trade union membership, health or sexual life. PIUs are also obliged to delete any such data if they receive it. These measures are important to ensure that the directive does not infringe on fundamental privacy rights.    **Therefore, Answer (a) is better.**    The concerns raised by the EDRI, FRA, and critics are valid and should be taken into consideration when implementing the new PNR directive. However, the directive does include important safeguards to protect privacy and prevent discrimination. By striking a balance between the need to combat crime and the protection of individual rights, the new PNR directive has the potential to be an effective tool in combating serious crime while safeguarding privacy.
